                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">تَمَّ الشَّىْءُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (T, S, M, K, &amp;c.,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar" marker="tami3a">تَمِمَ</orth>
                  </form>, (T, M, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَمَامٌ</foreign>, (T, S,) or <foreign lang="ar">تِمَامٌ</foreign>, (M,) or both, and <foreign lang="ar">تُمَامٌ</foreign>, (K,) and <foreign lang="ar">تَمَامَةٌ</foreign> (M, K) and <foreign lang="ar">تِمَامَةٌ</foreign>, (K,) and <foreign lang="ar">تمُّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">تَمٌّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">تُمٌّ</foreign>, (M, K,) of which last three forms the first is said to be the most chaste, (TA,) [<hi rend="ital">The thing was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, complete, entire, whole,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">full;</hi> i. e., <hi rend="ital">without,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">free from, deficiency:</hi> and sometimes, <hi rend="ital">the thing was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, consummate,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">perfect;</hi> which latter signification is more properly expressed by <foreign lang="ar">كَمَلَ</foreign>:] accord. to the author of the K, as is shown in art. <foreign lang="ar">كمل</foreign>, and accord. to some others, <foreign lang="ar">تَمَامٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كَمَالٌ</foreign> are syn.; but several authors make a distinction between them: the former is said to signify a thing's <hi rend="ital">being,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">becoming, without,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">free from, deficiency;</hi> and the latter, to signify <foreign lang="ar">تمام</foreign> and something more, as, for instance, goodliness, and excellence, essential or accidental; though each is sometimes used in the sense of the other: or, as some say, the former necessarily implies previous deficiency; but the latter does not: (MF, TA:) or, accord. to El-Harállee, the latter signifies the attaining to the utmost point, or degree, in every respect: or, as Ibn-El-Kemál says, when one says of a thing <foreign lang="ar">كَمَلَ</foreign>, he means that what was desired of it became realized. (TA.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">تَمَامٌ</foreign>, below.] You say, <foreign lang="ar">تَمَّ خَلْقُهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">His make,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">formation, was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, complete,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">perfect; he</hi> (a child or the like, and a man,) <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, fully formed</hi> or <hi rend="ital">developed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">complete in his members;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">he</hi> (a man) <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, full-grown</hi>]: (TA:) [whence, probably,] <foreign lang="ar">تَمَّ الشَّىْءُ</foreign> [as meaning] <hi rend="ital">The thing became strong and hard.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">تَمَّ القَمَرُ</foreign>, (T, S, Msb,) or   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n4077-1" target="اتمّ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n4080"/></foreign>, (M, K,) <hi rend="ital">The moon became full, so that it shone brightly.</hi> (M, K) And, of her who is pregnant, <foreign lang="ar">تَمَّتْ أَيَّامُ حَمْلِهَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The days of her gestation became complete</hi>]. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">تَمَّ إِلَى كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He reached, attained, arrived at,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came to, such a thing;</hi> as, for instance, eminence or nobility, or the means of acquiring eminence or nobility. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">تَمَّ إِلَى مَوْضِعِ كَذَا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n4077-2" target="اتمّ" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n4080"/>إِلَيْهِ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He repaired,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">betook himself, to,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">towards, such a place; he went to it.</hi> (Har p. 508.) Aboo-Dhu-eyb says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">فَبَاتَ بِجَمْعٍ ثُمَّ تَمَّ إِلَى مِنًى</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [which may be rendered <hi rend="ital">And he passed the night in Jema</hi> (a name of El-Muzdelifeh): <hi rend="ital">then he repaired,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">went, to Minè;</hi> there completing the ceremonies of the pilgrimage; wherefore ISd says,] I think that, by <foreign lang="ar">تمّ</foreign>, [or rather <foreign lang="ar">تمّ الى منى</foreign>,] he means <hi rend="ital">he completed his pilgrimage.</hi> (M.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">تَمَّ بِهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">تَمَّ عَلَيْهِ</foreign>: see their syn. <foreign lang="ar">اتمّهُ</foreign> (4).          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">تَمَّ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He performed it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">executed it; he accomplished it;</hi> namely, an affair; a fast; a purpose, or an intention. (Mgh.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">He persevered in it;</hi> (Mgh, TA;) as also <foreign lang="ar">تَمَمَ عَلَيْهِ</foreign>, without teshdeed, as in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">إِنْ تَمَمَتْ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَا أُرِيدُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">If she persevere in what I desire</hi>], occurring in a trad.; but IAth says that the verb here means   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n4077-3" target="تَمَّمَتْ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">تَمَّ عَلَى الإبَآءِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He persevered in refusal,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dislike,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">disapproval.</hi> (Mgh.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">تُمَّ</foreign>

                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">تَمِيمَةٌ</orth>

                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A kind of amulet</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">عُوذَةٌ</foreign>, T, S) <hi rend="ital">which is hung upon a human being;</hi> forbidden to be worn: (S:) or <hi rend="ital">a kind of bead:</hi> (S, Mgh:) erroneously imagined by some to be the same as <foreign lang="ar">مَعَاذَةٌ</foreign>: (El- Kutabee, Mgh:) but as to the <foreign lang="ar">مَعَاذَات</foreign> that are inscribed with something from the Kur-án, or with the names of God, in these there is no harm: (S, Mgh:) <hi rend="ital">a speckled bead, black speckled with white,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the reverse, which is strung upon a thong, and tied to the neck:</hi> (M, K:) sing. of <foreign lang="ar">تَمَائِمُ</foreign> and [n. un. of]   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n4097-1" target="تَمِيمٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n4094"/></foreign>: (T, M, K:) <foreign lang="ar">تَمَائِمُ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">certain beads which the Arabs of the desert used to hang upon their children, to repel, as they asserted, the evil eye:</hi> (T, Mgh:) or the <foreign lang="ar">تَمِيمَة</foreign> is, accord. to some, <hi rend="ital">a necklace</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">قِلَادَة</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">upon which are put thongs and amulets</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">عُوَذ</foreign>): (M:) or <hi rend="ital">a necklace</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">قِلَادَة</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">of thongs:</hi> and is sometimes applied to the <hi rend="ital">amulet</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">عُوذَة</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">that is hung upon the necks of children:</hi> (T:) but he who makes <foreign lang="ar">تمائم</foreign> to signify <hi rend="ital">thongs</hi> is in error: El-Farezdak uses the phrase <foreign lang="ar">سُيُورُ التَّمَائِمِ</foreign> because they are <hi rend="ital">beads which are perforated, and into which are inserted thongs or strings whereby they are suspended:</hi> (T, Mgh:) Az says, I have not found among the Arabs of the desert any difference of opinion respecting the <foreign lang="ar">تميمة</foreign>, as to its being the bead itself: (TA:) but accord. to En-Nakha'ee, the Prophet disapproved of everything hung upon a child or grown person, and said that all such things were <foreign lang="ar">تمائم</foreign>: (Mgh:) the <foreign lang="ar">تميمة</foreign> is [said to be] thus called because by it the condition of the child is rendered complete. (Har p. 22.)    </entryFree>2d:T98d,<entryFree id="n4100" key="تَامٌّ" type="main">
